# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0`, `github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0`, `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0`

# Service Deployment Pattern Discovery

## Your Task

Find the canonical patterns for deploying new services and how they are documented across repos. Specifically: 1. API type definition — Where is the authoritative `Deployment` struct defined in the Kubernetes API types repo? 2. Client-side code pattern — Where is the canonical Go code example showing how to create a Deployment using the client library? 3. Developer documentation — Where is the README or documentation file that explains the deployment workflow?

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've successfully completed the research task and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`. 

## Summary of Findings

I discovered the canonical patterns for deploying services across the Kubernetes ecosystem:

### 1. **API Type Definition** 
- **Location**: `github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0` → `apps/v1/types.go` (lines 358-373)
- **Key Type**: `Deployment` struct with composed `DeploymentSpec` (lines 375-418)
- **Details**: Includes fields for replicas, pod selector, pod template, deployment strategy, and progress deadline
- **Status**: v1 is the stable, production-ready API version

### 2. **Client-Side Code Pattern**
- **Location**: `github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0` → `examples/create-update-delete-deployment/main.go` (lines 65-99)
- **Pattern**: 
  1. Load kubeconfig and create Kubernetes client
  2. Get typed Deployments client for a namespace
  3. Construct a Deployment struct with ObjectMeta and Spec
  4. Call `Create()`, `Update()`, `List()`, and `Delete()` operations
- **Best Practice**: Use `retry.RetryOnConflict` for updates to handle conflicts from concurrent operations

### 3. **Developer Documentation**
- **README**: `github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0` → `examples/create-update-delete-deployment/README.md`
- **Content**: Explains the four fundamental CRUD operations with detailed examples and verification steps
- **Overview**: Documented in `examples/README.md` under "Basics" section

The answer.json file includes all relevant file paths, symbols, and a comprehensive narrative explaining how these patterns work together to form the canonical Deployment workflow.

This README explains the four fundamental operations: (1) Create a 2-replica Deployment with a selector matching pod labels, (2) Update the Deployment by modifying the replica count and container image using the retry pattern to handle conflicts, (3) List Deployments in a namespace, and (4) Delete the Deployment with foreground propagation policy. The examples/README.md provides an overview listing this example under the 'Basics' section as the entry point for managing resources with the Kubernetes API.\\n\\nThe retry pattern shown in the example (using retry.RetryOnConflict) is the recommended approach for updates, as it preserves changes made by other clients between Create and Update operations by fetching the latest version before modifying.\"\n}\n",

This is the v1 API version, which is the stable, production-ready version. The Deployment type composes metav1.TypeMeta, metav1.ObjectMeta for standard Kubernetes object metadata, and includes a DeploymentSpec (lines 375-418) that specifies the desired behavior including replicas, pod selector, pod template, deployment strategy, and progress deadline settings. The API repo's README.md documents that this is the canonical location of Kubernetes API definitions and should be used as a dependency through client-go.\\n\\n## Client-Side Code Pattern\\nThe canonical Go code example showing how to create a Deployment using the client library is in github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0 in examples/create-update-delete-deployment/main.go (lines 65-99). The example demonstrates the standard pattern: (1) Initialize a Kubernetes client using clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags, (2) Create a clientset via kubernetes.NewForConfig, (3) Get a typed Deployments client via clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(namespace), (4) Construct a *appsv1.Deployment struct with ObjectMeta (name) and Spec (replicas, selector, template with containers), and (5) Call deploymentsClient.Create(context.TODO(), deployment, metav1.CreateOptions{}). The example continues with update (using retry.RetryOnConflict to handle conflicts), list, and delete operations. The typed client interface is formally defined in kubernetes/typed/apps/v1/deployment.go and includes Create, Update, UpdateStatus, Delete, Get, List, Watch, and Patch methods.\\n\\n## Developer Documentation\\nThe deployment workflow documentation is located in github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0 at examples/create-update-delete-deployment/README.md. This README explains the four fundamental operations: (1) Create a 2-replica Deployment with a selector matching pod labels, (2) Update the Deployment by modifying the replica count and container image using the retry pattern to handle conflicts, (3) List Deployments in a namespace, and (4) Delete the Deployment with foreground propagation policy. The examples/README.md provides an overview listing this example under the 'Basics' section as the entry point for managing resources with the Kubernetes API.\\n\\nThe retry pattern shown in the example (using retry.RetryOnConflict) is the recommended approach for updates, as it preserves changes made by other clients between Create and Update operations by fetching the latest version before modifying.\"\n}\n",
